Note the free regions in the\n162: /// closure's signature and captures are erased.\n163: ///\n164: /// Example: If type check produces a closure with the closure args:\n165: ///\n166: /// ```text\n167: /// ClosureArgs = [\n168: ///     'a,                                         // From the parent.\n169: ///     'b,\n170: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n171: ///     for<'x> fn(&'<erased> &'x u32) -> &'x u32,  // the \"closure signature\"\n172: ///     &'<erased> String,                          // some upvar\n173: /// ]\n174: /// ```\n175: ///\n176: /// We would \"renumber\" each free region to a unique vid, as follows:\n177: ///\n178: /// ```text\n179: /// ClosureArgs = [\n180: ///     '1,                                         // From the parent.\n181: ///     '2,\n182: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n183: ///     for<'x> fn(&'3 &'x u32) -> &'x u32,         // the \"closure signature\"\n184: ///     &'4 String,                                 // some upvar\n185: /// ]\n186: /// ```\n187: ///\n188: /// Now the code might impose a requirement like `'1: '2`. When an\n189: /// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\n190: /// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\n191: /// outlives relationship.\n192: #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\n193: pub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\n194:     /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. In our\n195:     /// example above, it would be 3 -- one for `'static`, then `'1`\n196:     /// and `'2`. This is just used for a sanity check later on, to\n197:     /// make sure that the number of regions we see at the callsite\n198:     /// matches.\n199:     pub num_external_vids: usize,\n200: \n201:     /// Requirements between the various free regions defined in\n202:     /// indices.\n203:     pub outlives_requirements: Vec<ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx>>,\n204: }\n205: \n206: /// Indicates an outlives-constraint between a type or between two\n207: /// free regions declared on the closure.\n208: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n209: pub struct ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx> {\n210:     // This region or type ...\n211:     pub subject: ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx>,\n212: \n213:     // ... must outlive this one.\n214:     pub outlived_free_region: ty::RegionVid,\n215: \n216:     // If not, report an error here ...\n217:     pub blame_span: Span,\n218: \n219:     // ... due to this reason.\n220:     pub category: ConstraintCategory<'tcx>,\n221: }\n222: \n223: // Make sure this enum doesn't unintentionally grow\n224: #[cfg(target_pointer_width = \"64\")]\n225: rustc_data_structures::static_assert_size!(ConstraintCategory<'_>, 16);\n226: \n227: /// The subject of a `ClosureOutlivesRequirement` -- that is, the thing\n228: /// that must outlive some region.\n229: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n230: pub enum ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx> {\n231:     /// Subject is a type, typically a type parameter, but could also\n232:     /// be a projection. Indicates a requirement like `T: 'a` being\n233:     /// passed to the caller, where the type here is `T`.\n234:     Ty(ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx>),\n235: \n236:     /// Subject is a free region from the closure. Indicates a requirement\n237:     /// like `'a: 'b` being passed to the caller; the region here is `'a`.\n238:     Region(ty::RegionVid),\n239: }\n240: \n241: /// Represents a `ty::Ty` for use in [`ClosureOutlivesSubject`].\n242: ///\n243: /// This abstraction is necessary because the type may include `ReVar` regions,\n244: /// which is what we use internally within NLL code, and they can't be used in\n245: /// a query response.\n246: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n247: pub struct ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n248:     inner: Ty<'tcx>,\n249: }\n250: // DO NOT implement `TypeVisitable` or `TypeFoldable` traits, because this\n251: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/lib.rs%3FL100-250"}}}

The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! Then our steps are:\\n33: //! ```text\\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n37: //! ```\\n38: //!\\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - We only need\n73: // to compute whether a variable `X` is live if that variable contains\n74: // some region `R` in its type where `R` is not known to outlive a free\n75: // region (i.e., where `R` may be valid for just a subset of the fn body).\n76: fn compute_relevant_live_locals<'tcx>(\n77:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n78:     free_regions: &FxHashSet<RegionVid>,\n79:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\n80: ) -> (Vec<Local>, Vec<Local>) {\n81:     let (boring_locals, relevant_live_locals): (Vec<_>, Vec<_>) =\n82:         body.local_decls.iter_enumerated().partition_map(|(local, local_decl)| {\n83:             if tcx.all_free_regions_meet(&local_decl.ty, |r| free_regions.contains(&r.as_var())) {\n84:                 Either::Left(local)\n85:             } else {\n86:                 Either::Right(local)\n87:             }\n88:         });\n89: \n90:     debug!(\"{} total variables\", body.local_decls.len());\n91:     debug!(\"{} variables need liveness\", relevant_live_locals.len());\n92:     debug!(\"{} regions outlive free regions\", free_regions.len());\n93: \n94:     (relevant_live_locals, boring_locals)\n95: }\n96: \n97: /// Computes all regions that are (currently) known to outlive free\n98: /// regions. For these regions, we do not need to compute\n99: /// liveness, since the outlives constraints will ensure that they\n100: /// are live over the whole fn body anyhow.\n101: fn regions_that_outlive_free_regions<'tcx>(\n102:     num_region_vars: usize,\n103:     universal_regions: &UniversalRegions<'tcx>,\n104:     constraint_set: &OutlivesConstraintSet<'tcx>,\n105: ) -> FxHashSet<RegionVid> {\n106:     // Build a graph of the outlives constraints thus far. This is\n107:     // a reverse graph, so for each constraint `R1: R2` we have an\n108:     // edge `R2 -> R1`. Therefore, if we find all regions\n109:     // reachable from each free region, we will have all the\n110:     // regions that are forced to outlive some free region.\n111:     let rev_constraint_graph = constraint_set.reverse_graph(num_region_vars);\n112:     let fr_static = universal_regions.fr_static;\n113:     let rev_region_graph = rev_constraint_graph.region_graph(constraint_set, fr_static);\n114: \n115:     // Stack for the depth-first search. Each of the points in the\n37: /// DROP-LIVE set are to the liveness sets for regions found in the\n38: /// `dropck_outlives` result of the variable's type (in particular,\n39: /// this respects `#[may_dangle]` annotations).\n40: pub(super) fn trace<'tcx>(\n41:     typeck: &mut TypeChecker<'_, 'tcx>,\n42:     location_map: &DenseLocationMap,\n43:     move_data: &MoveData<'tcx>,\n44:     relevant_live_locals: Vec<Local>,\n45:     boring_locals: Vec<Local>,\n46: ) {\n47:     let local_use_map = &LocalUseMap::build(&relevant_live_locals, location_map, typeck.body);\n48:     let cx = LivenessContext {\n49:         typeck,\n50:         flow_inits: None,\n51:         location_map,\n52:         local_use_map,\n53:         move_data,\n54:         drop_data: FxIndexMap::default(),\n55:     };\n56: \n57:     let mut results = LivenessResults::new(cx);\n58: \n59:     results.add_extra_drop_facts(&relevant_live_locals);\n60: \n61:     results.compute_for_all_locals(relevant_live_locals);\n62: \n63:     results.dropck_boring_locals(boring_locals);\n64: }\n65: \n66: /// Contextual state for the type-liveness coroutine.\n67: struct LivenessContext<'a, 'typeck, 'tcx> {\n68:     /// Current type-checker, giving us our inference context etc.\n69:     ///\n70:     /// This also stores the body we're currently analyzing.\n71:     typeck: &'a mut TypeChecker<'typeck, 'tcx>,\n72: \n73:     /// Defines the `PointIndex` mapping\n74:     location_map: &'a DenseLocationMap,\n75: \n76:     /// Mapping to/from the various indices used for initialization tracking.\n77:     move_data: &'a MoveData<'tcx>,\n78: \n79:     /// Cache for the results of `dropck_outlives` query.\n80:     drop_data: FxIndexMap<Ty<'tcx>, DropData<'tcx>>,\n81: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/type_check/liveness/trace.rs%3FL1-80"}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_0122to68utEfNecsscTkPmka","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"55:             }\\n56:         }\\n57:     }\\n58: }\\n59: \\n60: pub(super) fn is_active<'tcx>(\\n61:     dominators: &Dominators<BasicBlock>,\\n62:     borrow_data: &BorrowData<'tcx>,\\n63:     location: Location,\\n64: ) -> bool {\\n65:     debug!(\\\"is_active(borrow_data={:?}, location={:?})\\\", borrow_data, location);\\n66: \\n67:     let activation_location = match borrow_data.activation_location {\\n68:         // If this is not a 2-phase borrow, it is always active.\\n69:         TwoPhaseActivation::NotTwoPhase => return true,\\n70:         // And if the unique 2-phase use is not an activation, then it is *never* active.\\n71:         TwoPhaseActivation::NotActivated => return false,\\n72:         // Otherwise, we derive info from the activation point `loc`:\\n73:         TwoPhaseActivation::ActivatedAt(loc) => loc,\\n74:     };\\n75: \\n76:     // Otherwise, it is active for every location *except* in between\\n77:     // the reservation and the activation:\\n78:     //\\n79:     //       X\\n80:     //      /\\n81:     //     R      <--+ Except for this\\n82:     //    / \\\\        | diamond\\n83:     //    \\\\ /        |\\n84:     //     A  <------+\\n85:     //     |\\n86:     //     Z\\n87:     //\\n88:     // Note that we assume that:\\n89:     // - the reservation R dominates the activation A\\n90:     // - the activation A post-dominates the reservation R (ignoring unwinding edges).\\n91:     //\\n92:     // This means that there can't be an edge that leaves A and\\n93:     // comes back into that diamond unless it passes through R.\\n94:     //\\n95:     // Suboptimal: In some cases, this code walks the dominator\\n96:     // tree twice when it only has to be walked once.
